Kyra Guy

Problem 1: Vectorization

Original Code

fun1 <- function(n = 100, k = 4, lambda = 4) {
  x <- NULL
  
  for (i in 1:n){
    x <- rbind(x, rpois(k, lambda))    
  }
  
  return(x)
}

Faster code

fun1alt <- function(n = 100, k = 4, lambda = 4) {
  x <- matrix(nrow = n, ncol = k)
  
  for (i in 1:n) {
    x[i, ] <- rpois(k, lambda)
  }
  
  return(x)
}

Check

set.seed(123)

n <- 100
k <- 4
lambda <- 4

Max value of each column

# Data Generating Process (10 x 10,000 matrix)
set.seed(1234)
x <- matrix(rnorm(1e4), nrow=10)

# Find each column's max value
fun2 <- function(x) {
  apply(x, 2, max)
}

fun2alt <- function(x) {
  max_indices <- max.col(x, "first")
  result <- x[cbind(1:nrow(x), max_indices)]
  return(result)
}

Check

set.seed(1234)

x <- matrix(rnorm(1e4), nrow = 10)

identical(fun2(x), fun2alt(x))
[1] FALSE
mbm <- microbenchmark(
  original = fun2(x),
  optimized = fun2alt(x),
  times = 100
)

Problem 3: Parallelization

library(parallel)

my_boot <- function(dat, stat, R, ncpus = 1L) {
  
  # Getting the random indices
  n <- nrow(dat)
  idx <- matrix(sample.int(n, n*R, TRUE), nrow=n, ncol=R)
  
  # PARALLELIZED VERSION USING MCLAPPLY
  ans <- mclapply(seq_len(R), function(i) {
    stat(dat[idx[, i], , drop=FALSE])
  }, mc.cores = ncpus)
  
  # Converting the list into a matrix
  ans <- do.call(rbind, ans)

  return(ans)
}

Check
